Saturday, 10:20 a.m. – Grand Prix Trial Winners (Standard)
----------------------------------------------------------


*by Tobi Henke*

 

As is tradition, the Friday was reserved for lots and lots of Grand Prix Trial tournaments, 32-player affairs which are single elimination and award three byes for the main event to the last one standing, to the brave soul who manages to win every last round, going 5-0.


Now, this weekend's main focus is of course on *Gatecrash* Limited. The Grand Prix has just begun with 1,970 players each building their own *Gatecrash* Sealed Deck, and tomorrow there will be *Gatecrash* Booster Draft. For the Trials, however, players had the option between Sealed and Standard. The majority decided to stick with 40 cards, but a few brought their 60-card decks. A new Limited environment is definitely exciting, but so is a new Constructed environment, even more so when that's what's being played at the Pro Tour just next week. Reason enough to take a look at the winning Standard decks, of which there were seven.


The influence of *Gatecrash* was all-encompassing, if only because of the new shocklands. While old favorites like Jund and Zombies continued to perform well, some very new creations showed promise too. For example, Thomas McVeigh combined Simic's [Zameck Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zameck+Guildmage) with [Strangleroot Geist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Strangleroot+Geist) and [Young Wolf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Young+Wolf) for a never-ending stream of creatures (and extra cards), whereas Jimmy Wild splashed [Geist of Saint Traft](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Geist+of+Saint+Traft) into an essentially mono-red deck. Curving out with [Rakdos Cackler](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rakdos+Cackler), [Ash Zealot](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ash+Zealot), and Geist seems downright unfair, especially when followed up by [Boros Charm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Boros+Charm) (and [Snapcaster Mage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Snapcaster+Mage) on [Boros Charm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Boros+Charm)). And Alexandre Aurejac apparently found a home for [Obzedat, Ghost Council](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Obzedat%2C+Ghost+Council). Check out there decks here!







#### Jimmy Wild

---



Saturday, 10:20 a.m. – Grand Prix Trial Winners (Sealed)
--------------------------------------------------------


*by Tobi Henke*

 

Now, let's take a look at some sealed decks, shall we? All of the following decks remained undefeated throughout yesterday's Trials, achieving records of 5-0. So what does it take to have a succesful sealed deck? What does one have to be on the lookout for?


In general, the format appears to be very aggressive, much more so than *Return to Ravnica*. Multicolor environments often tend toward the opposite, so it's rather refreshing to see the blisteringly fast openings some of these decks were capable of. Trial winner Tatu Junkkari for example included the whopping number of four one-drops in his deck! In combination with lots and lots of bloodthirst and [Act of Treason](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Act+of+Treason), he hardly needed any removal or big rare bombs. Likewise, most of the winners stayed away from adventurous splashes; half of the following decks are straight-up two colors, which is quite impressive considering the setting of Ravnica.







#### Tatu Junkkari


##### 






![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)

---



Saturday, 12:44 p.m. – Talking Sealed with Nico Bohny
-----------------------------------------------------


*by Tobi Henke*

 

Yesterday, when I got the first list of the early Grand Prix Trial winners, one name immediately caught my eye. Nico Bohny, the Grand Prix champion and two-time Pro Tour Top 8 competitor from Switzerland, had apparently made good use of his Friday. He tried to get in some additional experience with the new set and in the process earned himself three byes. So how did he approach the *Gatecrash* Sealed Deck format?


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gplon13/blog_bohny.jpg)*Nico Bohny*
 

"I'm by no means an expert. I wasn't sure about a lot of the cards," Bohny admitted. "For example, do you want to include [Smite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Smite) in a somewhat aggressive deck with bloodrush? How good is [Towering Thunderfist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Towering+Thunderfist)? Or [Ruination Wurm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ruination+Wurm)? I ended up with one Wurm, one Thunderfist, and one [Smite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Smite) in my deck and another one of each in my sideboard.


"Basically, I tried to steer clear of anything too extreme. Some sealed pools allow for rather narrow aggro strategies, or sometimes players will try to go big. I wanted to stay in the middle of the road and build a more, let's call it, 'well-rounded' deck, a typical sealed deck really, instead of something splashy and potentially spectacular."







#### Nico Bohny


##### 






![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)

99 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Forest)


















 

Nevertheless, his deck did include some nifty combos. "Poor me, I never actually drew [Biomass Mutation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Biomass+Mutation) when I had [Assemble the Legion](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Assemble+the+Legion)," Bohny joked, "but a couple of times I managed to make all of my creatures indestructible with [Frontline Medic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Frontline+Medic) which really improved all those [Pit Fight](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Pit+Fight)s!"


With a 3-0 start into the tournament already secured, we might hear more from Bohny later on, although he didn't like his deck for the main event quite as much. "Awkward three-color mana base and more filler cards than I'm happy with. It's good that I have these byes, I guess. I really need them," he said.




---



Saturday, 2:04 p.m. – The Mystery Pool Challenge
------------------------------------------------


*by David Sutcliffe*

 

One of the most interesting things you get to do in coverage at a Grand Prix is test your deckbuilding skills against those of some of the best players in the world. Would you have made the same decisions, given the same cards?


This is a sealed *Gatecrash* pool that has fallen into the hands of a veteran European pro player, and former Grand Prix champion. We're not going to tell you who that is right now – we'll catch up with him later and let him tell you how he built his pool – but in the meantime there's a game that you can all play along with at home.


So here's your challenge: given these six boosters, what's your guild? Do you have a splash? Is it good? Are you going to make Day Two with this deck?


Let us know how you build it on Twitter at @magicprotour with the #gplondon tag.


 [![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/magic/sealeddeckbuilder/assets/Frontloader-Preview.jpg)](http://www.wizards.com/magic/sealeddeckbuilder/index.html?draftid=gplon13a)
[![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/activity/sealedDeckBuilderButton_Static.jpg)](http://www.wizards.com/magic/sealeddeckbuilder/index.html?draftid=gplon13a)


---



Saturday, 4:20 p.m. – Preparing for the Pro Tour
------------------------------------------------


*by Tobi Henke*

 

Hall of Famer Paulo Vitor Damo da Rosa is a busy man, playing a Grand Prix this weekend, a Pro Tour next weekend, with testing in between. Fortunately, he has quite a bit of help from his teammates at ChannelFireball.


"The other guys already met, basically everyone but Martin [Jůza] and me. They're doing a lot of drafts over in the U.S., we're doing a lot of drafts here, and on Monday we're meeting in Montreal for lots and lots of Constructed testing," said Paulo. "It is a little pressed on time which isn't ideal, but Martin and I wanted to play this event here, so what can you do."


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gplon13/blog_da_rosa.jpg)*Paulo Vitor Damo da Rosa*
 

"I haven't done any Constructed testing so far," Paulo admitted. "Right now nothing's narrowed down yet, Standard's still wide open."


Austria's Platinum pro Thomas Holzinger has his Pro Tour testing all planned out, apparently. "We figured, it's going to be awfully cold in Montreal, so we're going to spend a lot of time indoors. Basically, we're all set then, aren't we?" he joked. More seriously he mentioned that he's testing with almost almost all the Austrians and Germans, including Grand Prix Moscow finalist Wenzel Krautmann, three-time GP Top 8er Klaus Jöns, and Worlds runner-up David Reitbauer.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gplon13/blog_holzinger.jpg)*Thomas Holzinger*
 

"We've already tested some, but there are still a number of crazy ideas for Standard decks floating around." Pressed for specifics, Holzinger was hesitant not to reveal too much, of course, but decided he could safely disclose the following: "For example, I just learned yesterday of the rather realistic possibility of infinite life in Standard. [Boros Reckoner](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Boros+Reckoner), in combination with either [Boros Charm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Boros+Charm) or [Frontline Medic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Frontline+Medic) for indestructibility and either [Nearheath Pilgrim](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nearheath+Pilgrim) or [Swift Justice](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swift+Justice) for lifelink, only needs to get some damage to then repeatedly damage itself, gaining arbitrary amounts of life in the process."




---



Round 4 Feature Match – David Reitbauer vs. Christian Calcano
-------------------------------------------------------------


*by David Sutcliffe*

 

Christian Calcano was part of a small but elite contingent of players who had travelled across the Atlantic to play in Grand Prix London, before flying straight back for Pro Tour Montreal. The travelling gunslinger has landed tough opposition in the fourth round here in London, however, facing off against the Austrian David Reitbauer – runner up in the 2009 World Championships


Winning the dice roll, Calcano declared his guild affiliation with an [Orzhov Guildgate](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Orzhov+Guildgate) before playing Pristmatic Prism, while Reitbauer began the evolution of his Simic forces with a [Gyre Sage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gyre+Sage), although the Elf Druid didn't gain a +1/+1 counter from the arrival of a [Metropolis Sprite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Metropolis+Sprite) on the Austrian's next turn. Calcano played a [Knight of Obligation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+Obligation), then after Reitbauer passed the turn the American revealed a tricky Dimir splash to his deck – a [Call of the Nightwing](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Call+of+the+Nightwing) that resolved, then was imprinted onto the [Knight of Obligation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+Obligation) before an attack.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gplon13/Round-4-Calcano.jpg)*Christian Calcano*
 

Two flying horrors sprang to Calcano's side, Reitbauer deployed a [Leyline Phantom](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Leyline+Phantom) as a deterrent but on his next turn Calcano played a [Holy Mantle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Holy+Mantle) onto his [Knight of Obligation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+Obligation), even finding time to pay for Extort! The [Knight of Obligation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+Obligation) had become a one-man army – a 4/6 creature with Vigiliance, Extort, Protection from Creatures, and the Ciphered ability to spawn more batwinged terrors with every unblockable attack!


Reitbauer threw down dudes as fast as he could – a [Drakewing Krasis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Drakewing+Krasis) and [Ooze Flux](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ooze+Flux) joined his team alongside the [Metropolis Sprite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Metropolis+Sprite), [Leyline Phantom](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Leyline+Phantom) and 3/4 [Gyre Sage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gyre+Sage), but Simic's creature-based strategy was poorly matched against [Holy Mantle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Holy+Mantle). Calcano wasted little time in pressing the advantage, sending the [Knight of Obligation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+Obligation) and a swarm of tokens at the Austrian – that put the scores at 5 life to 21, and Calcano could then pay to Extort the copy of [Call of the Nightwing](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Call+of+the+Nightwing), and a [Death's Approach](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Death%27s+Approach), swinging the life totals even further in his favor.


3 life now played 23, and Reitbauer needed his next card to be something that could kill [Knight of Obligation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+Obligation) before he could swing again. It wasn't, and Christian Calcano wrapped up a dominant first game win.



![Zameck Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Zameck+Guildmage)

David Reitbauer 0 – 1 Christian Calcano


On the play in the second game, Reitbauer made a quicker start with [Zameck Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zameck+Guildmage) and [Drakewing Krasis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Drakewing+Krasis) putting Calcano on his heels. The American responded with [Kingpin's Pet](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kingpin%27s+Pet) but opted not to trade, dropping to 13 life on the next attack before hitting back with [Basilica Guards](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Basilica+Guards), paying to Extort, then swinging the Pet back at Reitbauer.


The stage was set – Reitbauer was going to attempt to blow Calcano out of the water, and Calcano was intending to race back with the help of his Orzhov extortionists!


The Austrian swung again, the [Zameck Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zameck+Guildmage) bouncing off Calcano's [Basilica Guards](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Basilica+Guards) but dealing 3 with [Drakewing Krasis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Drakewing+Krasis), then added the tricky threat of a [Simic Manipulator](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Simic+Manipulator). Calcano took time out to read the Manipulator and absorb it's impact on his plan before attacking once again with [Kingpin's Pet](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Kingpin%27s+Pet) and adding a third Extort creature – a [Crypt Ghast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crypt+Ghast).


The Extort was starting to work in Calcano's favour, and despite the offense Reitbauer was barely ahead on life at 14-12. The Austrian now displayed his big play to steal the game – a [Clinging Anemones](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Clinging+Anemones) that Evolved the [Simic Manipulator](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Simic+Manipulator), then used Rapid Hybridisation to immediately turn the Anemones into a bizarre 3/3 Frog Lizard, adding another +1/+1 to the Manipulator. Ending his turn by stealing Calcano's [Crypt Ghast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crypt+Ghast) with [Simic Manipulator](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Simic+Manipulator), Reitbauer looked in good shape.


Calcano replied with a [Vizkopa Confessor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vizkopa+Confessor), paying 1 life to remove the last card from Reitbauer's hand – a chunky [Sylvan Primordial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sylvan+Primordial). This was even more Extort on the American's side of the table, but while his creatures were keeping the American in the game they were all potential victims of the [Simic Manipulator](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Simic+Manipulator).


Calcano did have a handy creature waiting in the wings, though – an [Undercity Informer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Undercity+Informer) that was more than happy to sacrifice any creature the [Simic Manipulator](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Simic+Manipulator) wanted to take. The Informer saw immediate use on Reitbauer's next turn, sending the [Basilica Guards](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Basilica+Guards) to meet their maker as Reitbauer played a [Stolen Identity](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Stolen+Identity) to create another 3/3 Frog Lizard. The [Vizkopa Confessor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vizkopa+Confessor) suffered the same fate a turn later, and while the [Simic Manipulator](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Simic+Manipulator) was not stealing Calcano's creature it was still able to ensure their sacrifice. The Manipulator meant that Reitbauer edged further and further ahead, adding a 3/4 [Gyre Sage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gyre+Sage) thanks to a double activation of [Zameck Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zameck+Guildmage).


Calcano was on his knees – hurling [Undercity Informer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Undercity+Informer) at an attacker meant his remaining [Gutter Skulk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gutter+Skulk) was no match for the army of Simic spawn at Reitbauer's command. Drawing a final card, the American scooped up what few cards he had left in play and we were into a decisive third game.


David Reitbauer 1 – 1 Christian Calcano



![Devour Flesh](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Devour+Flesh)

Reitbauer's victory in the second game had been just as assured as Calcano's sweep of the first and both players clearly had decks capable of imposing themselves on the opponent. This third game began more tentatively, though, with Calcano slow to start before using [Devour Flesh](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Devour+Flesh) to kill [Zameck Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zameck+Guildmage). A [Drakewing Krasis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Drakewing+Krasis) took Reitbauer's fight to the air, while Calcano turned to [Crypt Ghast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crypt+Ghast).


A [Keymaster Rogue](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Keymaster+Rogue) replaced the [Drakewing Krasis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Drakewing+Krasis) on the Austrian's next turn, but that seemed to be a stumbled tempo play for the Simic deck's beatdown, and Reitbauer had to brace for the impact of what Calcano could do with all the mana he would gain from the [Crypt Ghast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crypt+Ghast).


First out of Calcano's hand was a [Vizkopa Confessor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vizkopa+Confessor) with the American bravely paying 5 life to look at Reitbauer's entire hand, taking [Hands of Binding](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hands+of+Binding) from a choice of [Drakewing Krasis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Drakewing+Krasis), [Metropolis Sprite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Metropolis+Sprite), [Elusive Krasis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elusive+Krasis) and [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island). Reitbauer threw down his [Elusive Krasis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elusive+Krasis) and [Metropolis Sprite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Metropolis+Sprite), but with Calcano now having two Extort creatures the offensive was slow going, and a [Deathcult Rogue](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathcult+Rogue) arrived with double-Extort from the [Crypt Ghast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crypt+Ghast) and [Vizkopa Confessor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vizkopa+Confessor).


Calcano's defences remained far from watertight, and it was starting to look as though his decision to pay 5 life with [Vizkopa Confessor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Vizkopa+Confessor) had fallen on the wrong side of 'brave' as his opponent's foot remained glued to the accelerator. An [Experiment One](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Experiment+One) and [Drakewing Krasis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Drakewing+Krasis) joined the fray, adding a second +1/+1 counter to the [Elusive Krasis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elusive+Krasis). Between the Krasis and the [Keymaster Rogue](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Keymaster+Rogue) Reitbauer now had 5 power of unblockable creatures, with the Metropolis Spirite joining the fight to swing for 7 damage.


After taking that beating on the chin Calcano was 17-5 down on life and needed some big Extort action to fend off the coming onslaught. A [Balustrade Spy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Balustrade+Spy) offered some flying defense and an opportunity for extortion, before [Gift of Orzhova](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gift+of+Orzhova) added some crucial [Lifelink](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Lifelink) to the [Deathcult Rogue](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathcult+Rogue) – attacking for 3 with his Rogue, Calcano had managed to swing the lifetotals to a more respectable 12-10 in a single turn!


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gplon13/Round-4-Reitbauer.jpg)*David Reitbauer*
 

Reitbauer was unphased, though – he drew a card, paused for a brief piece of combat math, then delivered a strike with all his creatures. Calcano could have no answer to the [Elusive Krasis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elusive+Krasis) or [Keymaster Rogue](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Keymaster+Rogue) but hurled the [Balustrade Spy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Balustrade+Spy) in front of [Drakewing Krasis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Drakewing+Krasis), leaving [Metropolis Sprite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Metropolis+Sprite) unblocked.


It was enough for the American to survive another turn... or so it seemed! Before damage was dealt David Reitbauer revealed one final trick – a Bloodrushed's [Scab-Clan Charger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scab-Clan+Charger) gave +2/+4 to his [Metropolis Sprite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Metropolis+Sprite), and he then transferred two of that Toughness to Power with the Sprite's ability. A 5/4 Sprite, 2/6 [Elusive Krasis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elusive+Krasis) and 3/2 [Keymaster Rogue](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Keymaster+Rogue) meant 10 unblocked damage, and that was the match!


**David Reitbauer 2 – 1 Christian Calcano**




---



Round 5 Feature Match – Samuele Estratti vs. Stanislav Cifka
------------------------------------------------------------


*by Tobi Henke*

 

Nearly halfway through day one, neither of the players had picked up any losses so far, but the hardest part was yet to come, beginning with this match right here. Pro Tour Philadelphia champion Samuele Estratti had built an aggressive Boros deck, while Pro Tour *Return to Ravnica* champion Stanislav Cifka brought a blue-red-green deck with a splash of white.


### Game 1


Estratti won the die-roll and opened on [Daring Skyjek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daring+Skyjek) and [Court Street Denizen](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Court+Street+Denizen), while Cifka cast a pair of [Disciple of the Old Ways](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Disciple+of+the+Old+Ways) (without red mana). On turn four, Estratti summoned [Skyknight Legionnaire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Skyknight+Legionnaire), tapped one of the opposing 2/2s, thought a while about his attack, then attacked with just the Legionnaire.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gplon13/fm5_estratti.jpg)*Samuele Estratti*
 

Cifka made Verdant Harvest and [Skarrg Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Skarrg+Guildmage), Estratti exiled the latter with [Angelic Edict](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Angelic+Edict) and got in for another 2. Cifka cast [Prophetic Prism](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Prophetic+Prism) and [Zameck Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zameck+Guildmage) and passed the turn back to Estratti, who attacked for 2 more damage and added [Warmind Infantry](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Warmind+Infantry) to his team.


Cifka summoned [Ruination Wurm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ruination+Wurm), his first real threat since [Gruul Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gruul+Guildmage). Estratti drew his sixth land and had a better six-drop in [Urbis Protector](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Urbis+Protector). The two white creatures allowed [Court Street Denizen](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Court+Street+Denizen) to tap most of Cifka's defense, and [Warmind Infantry](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Warmind+Infantry), [Skyknight Legionnaire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Skyknight+Legionnaire), and [Daring Skyjek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daring+Skyjek) attacked for 9. Cifka had no answer for Estratti's fliers and that was that.


Samuele Estratti 1-0 Stanislav Cifka


### Game 2


Cifka started with [Cloudfin Raptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cloudfin+Raptor) followed by [Ember Beast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ember+Beast), Estratti had [Skinbrand Goblin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Skinbrand+Goblin) followed by [Bomber Corps](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Bomber+Corps). Estratti had a third creature in [Viashino Shanktail](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Viashino+Shanktail), Cifka summoned [Zameck Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zameck+Guildmage) growing his [Cloudfin Raptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cloudfin+Raptor) to 2/3.


This kept Estratti's [Skyknight Legionnaire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Skyknight+Legionnaire), played post combat, from attacking, but not his [Viashino Shanktail](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Viashino+Shanktail), which brought Cifka to 13. Cifka passed the turn without play. Estratti feared a trap and held back, cast an [Assault Griffin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Assault+Griffin) and passed himself. At end of turn, Cifka drew a card off [Zameck Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zameck+Guildmage), removing one counter from [Cloudfin Raptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cloudfin+Raptor), then cast [Shambleshark](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Shambleshark) and on his turn [Ruination Wurm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ruination+Wurm), turning [Cloudfin Raptor](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cloudfin+Raptor) into a 3/4.


Estratti's [Assault Griffin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Assault+Griffin) and [Skyknight Legionnaire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Skyknight+Legionnaire) attacked, and his [Arrows of Justice](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Arrows+of+Justice) killed the Raptor. Afterwards, he played [Boros Elite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Boros+Elite) and was looking to be in very good position, ahead on life and creatures. However, Cifka turned all of his creatures ([Ember Beast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ember+Beast), [Zameck Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zameck+Guildmage), 3/2 [Shambleshark](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Shambleshark), and [Ruination Wurm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ruination+Wurm)) sideways and ended the game on the spot with a bloodrushed [Skarrg Goliath](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Skarrg+Goliath)!


Samuele Estratti 1-1 Stanislav Cifka


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gplon13/fm5_cifka.jpg)*Stanislav Cifka*
 

### Game 3


Estratti took mulligans down to five and wasn't able to mount much of an early offense. Or defense. He was still stuck on two lands (and one [Boros Elite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Boros+Elite)), when Cifka had already cast [Metropolis Sprite](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Metropolis+Sprite), [Crocanura](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crocanura), [Disciple of the Old Ways](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Disciple+of+the+Old+Ways), [Ember Beast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ember+Beast) and [Zameck Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zameck+Guildmage) (in that order). A [Martial Glory](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Martial+Glory) and a [Skinbrand Goblin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Skinbrand+Goblin) came way too late to make a difference and a third land never showed.


**Samuele Estratti 1-2 Stanislav Cifka**




---



Round 5 Feature Match – Samuele Estratti vs. Stanislav Cifka
------------------------------------------------------------


*by David Sutcliffe*

 


![Obzedat, Ghost Council](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Obzedat%2C+Ghost+Council)

With the hard graft of Sealed pool building behind them the attention of many players turned towards the **Magic** dealers here at Grand Prix London. With nearly 2,000 players in attendance it's a good job there are no less than four dealer stands on hand to sate their cardboard desires.


The dealers are also a great source of information on what is or isn't selling from a new set, even if they're only occasionally the breaking news themselves (I'm thinking of times like the great [Hunted Wumpus](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Hunted+Wumpus) rush). After checking in with the other stores I pulled aside our semi-regular card hype consultant, Nigel from [Twiddle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Twiddle)s Keep, for some of the low down.


"The card people are asking for most is the [Boros Reckoner](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Boros+Reckoner), and then the new lands of course. There are a lot of Boros cards going out, so as well as the Reckoner there's [Frontline Medic](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Frontline+Medic), [Legion Loyalist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Legion+Loyalist), then [Aurelia, the Warleader](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Aurelia%2C+the+Warleader) and [Aurelia's Fury](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Aurelia%27s+Fury). Not as many [Aurelia's Fury](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Aurelia%27s+Fury) as I expected, though. We've noticed that it's Uncommons that people are chasing at the moment, not just rares, so the Keyrunes are really popular, as well as [Cartel Aristocrat](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Cartel+Aristocrat) and [Ghor-Clan Rampager](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ghor-Clan+Rampager)."


"The set is so new, I think people are waiting for it all to settle down so they can see what cards are good. That happens a lot when a set is very new and with the Pro Tour coming up people are looking for what cards are used there before they buy cards. That's normal – we saw a few years ago that when Brian Kibler won the Pro Tour it changed what cards were popular, and cards that people thought were really average before the Pro Tour became massively popular."  

(I imagine he means Pro Tour Honolulu, and cards like [Huntmaster of the Fells](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Huntmaster+of+the+Fells) – Dave)


Away from [Twiddle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Twiddle)s Keep the other traders all recounted similar stories, with [Boros Reckoner](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Boros+Reckoner) and shock lands the first things on everybody's list, although there were a few variations. At **Magic** Madhouse they had seen a lot of interest in 'the new [Dark Confidant](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dark+Confidant)': [Duskmantle Seer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Duskmantle+Seer), while both the Madhouse and JK Entertainment were struggling to keep [Obzedat, Ghost Council](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Obzedat%2C+Ghost+Council) in stock, with JK claiming "we're buying him in as often as we can, but they always sell within five minutes".


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gplon13/traders.jpg)
 

What the dealers could all agree on was that *Gatecrash* was an extremely popular set, with boosters flying off the shelves. Ahead of Pro Tour *Gatecrash* there are some firm fan favourites already established, but all eyes will be on what surprises the best minds in the game can throw up in Montreal. The best card in *Gatecrash* may, even now, be lurking unseen and unloved... waiting for the chance to shine.




---



Round 7 Feature Match – Gregor Strubelj vs. Raphaël Lévy
--------------------------------------------------------


*by David Sutcliffe*

 

Raphaël Lévy is a freak of **Magic** evolution – he's the Pro Player design that was so good it has managed to survive every change of environment thrown at it. And Lévy doesn't just survive: more often than not, he thrives. New sets, new players, new rules, the Frenchman just adapts and survives at the top of the game when all of his contemporaries have been and gone. Lévy admits that he can't dedicate the hours to learning constructed formats and be as competitive as he would like, but given a brand new Sealed format his lifetime of experience makes him one of the fastest learners, and one of the most dangerous opponents. The veteran of veterans was proving that fact once again in London, taking a 6-0 record into his feature match against his Slovenian opponent, Gregor Strubelj


Strubelj opened with an unfortunate mulligan but still took the front foot, laying a [Gutter Skulk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gutter+Skulk), [Basilica Guards](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Basilica+Guards) and [Syndicate Enforcer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Syndicate+Enforcer) unopposed, while Lévy laid only a trio of [Swamp](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Swamp)s and an [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island) before playing his first creature – a [Balustrade Spy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Balustrade+Spy). The Spy blocked the incoming [Syndicate Enforcer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Syndicate+Enforcer) but Strubelj simply replaced his lost Enforcer with a [Crypt Ghast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crypt+Ghast), trading one Extort creature for another. Lévy dropped a [Death's Approach](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Death%27s+Approach) onto the [Crypt Ghast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crypt+Ghast), but only gave it -1/-1: leaving open 1UB it seemed like Lévy was telegraphing a [Psychic Strike](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Psychic+Strike), but if so then Gregor Strubelj hadn't got the message and he sank all his mana into casting a big [Sapphire Drake](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sapphire+Drake) with double Extort. Lévy hadn't been bluffing the [Psychic Strike](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Psychic+Strike) and the Slovenian ran headlong into. That meant the [Sapphire Drake](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sapphire+Drake) was countered, which was a second creature into his graveyard, and in turn that meant [Death's Approach](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Death%27s+Approach) finally accounted for his [Crypt Ghast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crypt+Ghast) into the bargain.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gplon13/Round-7-Strubelj.jpg)*Gregor Strubelj*
 

That 2-for-1 swap was a painful loss of tempo for the Slovenian, but Strubelj was undaunted and played down his final two cards – a High priest of [Penance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Penance) and a [Smog Elemental](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Smog+Elemental). Lévy was down to 10 life after the early offense, but now stabilised behind a [Mindeye Drake](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mindeye+Drake) and [Corpse Blockade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Corpse+Blockade), before adding a [Sapphire Drake](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sapphire+Drake) of his own, and then his own [Crypt Ghast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crypt+Ghast)! With the immediate threat blunted a second [Death's Approach](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Death%27s+Approach) accounted for Strubelj's [Smog Elemental](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Smog+Elemental) and the game rapidly turned on its head – it was now Lévy in beatdown mode, and Lévy using Extort to rebuild his lifetotal.


Strubelj was rocking and could do nothing in the face of Lévy's onslaught, finally feeling that loss of a card to his early mulligan. The French veteran imprinted his [Mindeye Drake](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mindeye+Drake) with [Last Thoughts](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Last+Thoughts), sucking up more cards to trigger Extort. It was over, and Gregor Strubelj collected his cards.



![Wight of Precinct Six](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Wight+of+Precinct+Six)

Gregor Strubelj 0 – 1 Raphaël Lévy


After a glacial start in the first game Raphaël Lévy was quicker off the mark in the second – his [Wight of Precinct Six](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wight+of+Precinct+Six) might only have been a 1/1 to begin with but rapidly got [Tarmogoyf](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Tarmogoyf)-sized with the help of [Devour Flesh](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Devour+Flesh) and a [Balustrade Spy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Balustrade+Spy) that dug six cards into Strubelj's library, leaving the Wight a 3/3. The rot was setting in quickly and Strubelj needed defences, which he found with the combination of [Basilica Guards](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Basilica+Guards) and afflicting Lévy's Wight with [Agoraphobia](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Agoraphobia). In time, the Wight would get strong enough to no longer fear leaving the house, but it bought valuable time.


Lévy turned to aerial offense from his [Balustrade Spy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Balustrade+Spy), adding a [Deathcult Rogue](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathcult+Rogue) that would also prove tough to block. Strubelj had a [Crypt Ghast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crypt+Ghast) but that could only watch helplessly as Lévy's creatures slipped past into the red zone, to be joined by [Smog Elemental](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Smog+Elemental) on Lévy's next turn.


A [Mindeye Drake](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mindeye+Drake) was the first sign of real defense from Strubelj, but the Slovenian was still haemorrhaghing life with each passing turn and dropped to 11 life, with Lévy adding a second [Balustrade Spy](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Balustrade+Spy) to the assault. A [Sapphire Drake](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sapphire+Drake) finally became a flying blocker too many for Lévy, but that simply sent the veteran onto his next attack route and he played [Last Thoughts](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Last+Thoughts), imprinting it onto his [Deathcult Rogue](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathcult+Rogue) with Cipher before slipping in for another 2 damage and another card draw.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gplon13/Round-7-Levy.jpg)*Raphaël Lévy*
 

With most of the creatures on the table involved in a tense standoff the game moved into a new phase – Lévy could attack with [Deathcult Rogue](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathcult+Rogue) and draw cards, while Strubelj had three Extort creatures on the table. If he could keep a steady supply of spells to cast, there was a chance that Strubelj could battle his way out of the situation. As well as his draw step, Gregor Strubelj had one card he could rely on being able to cast: [Agoraphobia](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Agoraphobia), but when Lévy played [Corpse Blockade](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Corpse+Blockade) even that option went out the window as the French pro sacrificed his [Wight of Precinct Six](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Wight+of+Precinct+Six) before Strubelj could return the aura to hand!


Drawing an extra card each turn with [Last Thoughts](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Last+Thoughts) ensured that Lévy had all the answers – [Death's Approach](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Death%27s+Approach) removed the troublesome [Sapphire Drake](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sapphire+Drake) and cleared the way for another aerial assault. Taking 8 damage in one turn, Strubelj was battered down to 5 life... a triple-Extort while playing a second [Basilica Guards](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Basilica+Guards) hauled him back up to 8 but when a second [Death's Approach](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Death%27s+Approach) destroyed his [Mindeye Drake](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mindeye+Drake) Strubelj was left completely was defenceless, and Lévy's flyers wrapped up the match.


**Gregor Strubelj 0 – 2 Raphaël Lévy**




---



Saturday, 8:22 p.m. – Quick Question: Favorite Guild in Sealed Deck
-------------------------------------------------------------------


*by Tobi Henke*

 


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gplon13/blog_qq_eliaswatsfeldt.jpg)***Elias Watsfeldt**: Orzhov. I played four Sealeds and I've been Orzhov every single time. I also played against three Orzhov decks so far today.* 

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gplon13/blog_qq_dennizrachid.jpg)***Denniz Rachid**: For Sealed, I like something defensive, and I don't mind splashing. At the prerelease I played Orzhov splashing for double red cards, for example. So yeah, Orzhov with double-red splash, that's my favorite "guild."* 



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gplon13/blog_qq_paulovitordamodarosa.jpg)***Paulo Vitor Damo da Rosa**: Orzhov, I think. Or Gruul maybe. I really like both.* 

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gplon13/blog_qq_raphaellevy.jpg)***Raphaël Lévy**: Dimir. I'm playing Dimir today, and so far it's been amazing.* 




---



Saturday, 9:45 p.m. – Mystery Sealed Pool: The Final Deck Revealed
------------------------------------------------------------------


*by David Sutcliffe*

 

Earlier in the day [we shared a Mystery Sealed Pool with you](http://staging.wizards.com/Magic/Magazine/Article.aspx?x=mtg/daily/eventcoverage/gplon13/welcome#4) and asked you what deck you would make with that pool. The pool was one that had been given to a mystery Pro and Grand Prix Champion, and we can now reveal that the deck belonged to super-Swede Kenny Oberg.


Now comes the fun part – seeing how Kenny's picks from this pool differed from your own.


I don't know what you did with Kenny's pool, but the Swedish pro homed in on Gruul extremely quickly, quickly laying down the Green and Red cards from his pool, with a smaller pooler off to the side with some Boros splash cards to consider. The Gruul guild contained plenty of powerful cards, such as [Ruination Wurm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ruination+Wurm), [Zhur-Taa Swine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zhur-Taa+Swine) and the all-star [Clan Defiance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Clan+Defiance), but it also had a problem – the mana curve was all wrong, with only a clutch handful of cards he could play on the second turn. It was a cause for concern and Oberg ran back and forth through his options, only Boros appeared to offer a realistic option.


Extracting the green cards, Kenny dropped down his white ensemble in their place to see what a Boros option would look like, but it took just a few seconds for him to decide that [Zarichi Tiger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zarichi+Tiger) and [Dutiful Thrull](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Dutiful+Thrull) were no replacement for [Skarrg Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Skarrg+Guildmage) and [Ghor-Clan Rampager](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ghor-Clan+Rampager). The green went back in, and with a sole white splash for [Foundry Champion](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Foundry+Champion), Kenny Oberg was done with his deck and reached for his card sleeves.







#### Kenny Oberg


##### 






![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)

##### 2 (6)

1

[Foundry Champion](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BFoundry%5D+%5BChampion%5D)
