1
[Stomping Ground](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BStomping%5D+%5BGround%5D)


40 Cards 




![](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Boros+Guildgate)


















 

I steered Kenny away for a quiet chat, and first on the list was what he thought of his deck?


"I think I have a lot of cards that are below the average power level, but I have a lot of big creatures and that tends to win games of Sealed. My big weakness is that my mana curve isn't very good – I really needed a couple more two drops, or some more [Mugging](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mugging)s. The pool I registered then gave away had four [Mugging](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mugging)s in – I could have done with some of that!"


That didn't sound too promising, but Oberg saw lots of potential in his deck.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gplon13/Deckbuilding-Oberg.jpg)*Kenny Oberg*
 

"I have the [Gruul Keyrune](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gruul+Keyrune) and [Gyre Sage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gyre+Sage) and they could be really helpful in my deck, to get to my big creatures early. The [Gyre Sage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gyre+Sage) in particular can be really good, and I have two [Ivy Lane Denizen](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ivy+Lane+Denizen) to help me put more counters on the Sage. When he has +2/+2 he's really good, and when he has +3/+3 he's insane, and combos really well with Skargg Goliath. I think [Gyre Sage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gyre+Sage) may be the best card in my deck, because it plays all the roles I want it to play - even with just +1/+1 it's a good blocker with three toughness."



![Gyre Sage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Gyre+Sage)

[Gyre Sage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gyre+Sage) and [Skarrg Goliath](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Skarrg+Goliath) was an all-rare combo, but Kenny had praise for the combination of two commons in his deck as well.


"I really like [Madcap Skills](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Madcap+Skills) on an [Armored Transport](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Armored+Transport), that's a great combo. If they don't block the Transport they're dead really quickly, and if they do block it... it's like a double chump!"


From low beginnings, Kenny now seemed to be talking his deck up as a potential champ, so the Swede was sure to recognise the weaknesses as well and level the playing field.


"I have to be careful against quick decks, because I don't have those two drops - I nearly played the 1/1 red Denizen just as a sacrificial blocker. And I think an aggro deck with flyers could cause me real problems"


Moving away from the deck in hand, what practice had Kenny done for the Grand Prix?


"Not much – I'm concentrating on the Pro Tour next week! I played in a couple of Prerelease tournaments and I've done a few drafts as practice for the Pro Tour, but I haven't done any specific Sealed testing. The prerelease was really helpful in learning the cards, but with the Guild boosters it was almost like having two additional boosters to build from, so it's not too useful as practice. I played Orzhov and Simic in my prereleases so this is my first time with Gruul, although I did get the [Gyre Sage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gyre+Sage) and [Skarrg Goliath](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Skarrg+Goliath) combo in my Simic deck so I know how powerful that can be"


Who have you been practicing with for the Pro Tour?


"I've been working with all the Swedish guys who have qualified, like Denniz Rachid and Elias Watsfeldt – we've been sharing some ideas with the Finnish players as well. But really we plan to do most of the work once we get to Montreal – as always everything happens in the last week before a Pro Tour."


Without giving too much away, was *Gatecrash* going to have a big impact on Standard at the Pro Tour?


"Oh definitely! I don't think the impact is going to come in new decks, but there will be lots of improvements to existing decks. Just having those five extra shocklands gives players many more options for deckbuilding. The shocklands favour aggro decks though, so we'll have to see how that plays out"



![Clan Defiance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Clan+Defiance)

Kenny shared all those thoughts with me over six hours ago, when the deck was still fresh in his hands. How had he fared in the trials of combat?


After having such faith in his deck Kenny took a hit to his confidence when he found himself thrust straight into the live stream feature match in round 4, losing a tight match. Another narrow defeat followed in the next round, leaving the Swede on 3-2. But Oberg always believed his deck was better than that performance suggested and he charged back with three straight wins to head into Round 8 on a 5-2 record. Two more wins would carry Oberg into Day Two, but unfortunately a bad mana draw against a Boros deck with bad intentions saw Oberg blown away in Round Eight.


Catching Oberg on his exit from the tournament, what would he have changed?


"I've asked a lot of other players and they would have built the deck pretty much the same way, so I think I made it about as well as I could. The only thing I've sideboarded regularly is that I had a [Towering Thunderfist](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Towering+Thunderfist), and because I've been playing against Boros and Orzhov a lot they struggle to deal with it profitably. It's matchup-dependant, but maybe that would have been better than my [Adaptive Snapjaw](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Adaptive+Snapjaw) in the maindeck. But the games I lost were either really close, or in that last round he got the perfect cards against me – such as actually being able to counter [Clan Defiance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Clan+Defiance) with Field Medic in the first game, which pretty much never happens. That's **Magic**!"


With a philosophical air, Kenny Oberg bowed out of GP London... no doubt already thinking of Pro Tour *Gatecrash* next weekend.




---



Round 8 Feature Match – Shahar Shenhar vs. Nathalie Verly
---------------------------------------------------------


*by Tobi Henke*

 


![Court Street Denizen](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Court+Street+Denizen)

Both players were 6-1 so far, needing one more win to make it to the second day. Two-time Grand Prix champion Shahar Shenhar was on Orzhov, while Nathalie Verly had built a red-green-white deck.


### Game 1


Verly played first and started strong on [Burning-Tree Emissary](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Burning-Tree+Emissary) and [Skyknight Legionnaire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Skyknight+Legionnaire). Unfortunately, she had no immediate follow-up, while Shenhar summoned [Deathcult Rogue](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathcult+Rogue), [Basilica Guards](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Basilica+Guards), and [Court Street Denizen](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Court+Street+Denizen). Her [Rust Scarab](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rust+Scarab) fell victim to [Angelic Edict](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Angelic+Edict), and though both players had a creature the other couldn't block, Shenhar was pulling ahead in the damage race through [Basilica Guards](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Basilica+Guards)' extortion racket.


The small incremental advantage proved all but irrelevant, however, when Verly dropped the proverbial bomb: [Aurelia, the Warleader](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Aurelia%2C+the+Warleader) turned the damage race around, or rather the notion of any race at all on its head. Shenhar had no answer, and it didn't take long for Aurelia to end things.


Shahar Shenhar 0-1 Nathalie Verly


### Game 2


Both had slow starts, with just one creature until turn five: [Skyknight Legionnaire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Skyknight+Legionnaire) for Verly, [Gutter Skulk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gutter+Skulk) for Shenhar. [Skyknight Legionnaire](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Skyknight+Legionnaire) met [Devour Flesh](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Devour+Flesh) and was replaced with [Warmind Infantry](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Warmind+Infantry). Shenhar played a [Deathcult Rogue](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathcult+Rogue), then a second [Gutter Skulk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gutter+Skulk). Verly once again had [Aurelia, the Warleader](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Aurelia%2C+the+Warleader) which, together with [Warmind Infantry](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Warmind+Infantry), brought Shenhar in one sweep from 16 to 6. This time, however, Shenhar had [Angelic Edict](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Angelic+Edict) for the Angel.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gplon13/fm8_shenhar.jpg)*Shahar Shenhar*
 

Verly's [Warmind Infantry](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Warmind+Infantry) traded with one of the [Gutter Skulk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gutter+Skulk)s, but [Knight Watch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+Watch) and [Rust Scarab](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rust+Scarab) gave her plenty reinforcements. An attack plus [Massive Raid](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Massive+Raid) brought Shenhar to 1, but he recovered and slowly gained the upperhand. [Syndic of Tithes](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Syndic+of+Tithes) and [One Thousand Lashes](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=One+Thousand+Lashes) took care of the last 2/2 token and [Rust Scarab](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rust+Scarab), respectively, and soon Shenhar's [Deathcult Rogue](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathcult+Rogue) was back on offense, with an encoded [Undercity Plague](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Undercity+Plague) to boot!


Verly's [Assemble the Legion](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Assemble+the+Legion) came too late and didn't assemble or accomplish much of anything. [Deathcult Rogue](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathcult+Rogue) took the game.


Shahar Shenhar 1-1 Nathalie Verly


### Game 3


To start things off, [Greenside Watcher](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Greenside+Watcher) and [Gutter Skulk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gutter+Skulk) traded. Next, Verly had [Warmind Infantry](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Warmind+Infantry), then [Ember Beast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ember+Beast), but was left with no attackers, when the Infantry got stuck under [One Thousand Lashes](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=One+Thousand+Lashes). [Boros Keyrune](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Boros+Keyrune) and [Sunhome Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Sunhome+Guildmage), however, showed that Verly really was at no risk to run out of creatures.


Her [Massive Raid](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Massive+Raid) killed a freshly-summoned Guardian of the Guildless, and her Guildmage and [Ember Beast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ember+Beast) got in for 5. Shenhar summoned two [Basilica Guards](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Basilica+Guards). Verly swung in regardless, boosting her Guildmage to 4/2 to trade it off for one of the 1/4s.


Verly had yet more creatures, theoretically an infinite number even, in [Assemble the Legion](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Assemble+the+Legion), but only got one token before Shenhar exiled the enchantment with [Angelic Edict](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Angelic+Edict). Next, Shenhar cast [Gutter Skulk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gutter+Skulk), Verly cast [Knight of Obligation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+Obligation). Things weren't exactly looking good for Shenhar, and now Verly added another two creatures to her team with [Knight Watch](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+Watch).


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gplon13/fm8_verly.jpg)*Nathalie Verly*
 

At this point the board was: lands on both sides, two 2/2 tokens, one 1/1 token, [Knight of Obligation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+Obligation), [Ember Beast](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Ember+Beast), and [Boros Keyrune](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Boros+Keyrune) for Verly, a measly [Gutter Skulk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Gutter+Skulk) and [Basilica Guards](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Basilica+Guards) for Shenhar.


On her next turn, Verly swung with all of her creatures including [Boros Keyrune](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Boros+Keyrune). She lost [Knight of Obligation](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Knight+of+Obligation) to [Grisly Spectacle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grisly+Spectacle) and her 1/1 token to blocks but brought Shenhar to 2. He cast [Smog Elemental](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Smog+Elemental) and extorted to go to 3, then blocked so that he would survive on 1 life exactly ... barring unforeseen circumstances, of course, like Verly's [Slaughterhorn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Slaughterhorn), for example, bloodrushing to victory and to day two.


**Shahar Shenhar 1-2 Nathalie Verly**




---



Saturday, 10:29 p.m. – Quick Question: Pick Your Common
-------------------------------------------------------


*by Tobi Henke*

 

Let's say you could choose any one common from *Gatecrash* and have five copies of it in your next sealed pool. Which one would you pick?



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gplon13/blog_qq_eliaswatsfeldt.jpg)***Elias Watsfeldt**: Tough. I'm going to go with [Basilica Guards](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Basilica+Guards), but that's a personal preference. I'm sure it's not actually the best.* 

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gplon13/blog_qq_dennizrachid.jpg)***Denniz Rachid**: [Slaughterhorn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Slaughterhorn). It's a [Giant Growth](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Giant+Growth) that's also a creature. It depends a little on the number of one- and two-drops you have, but what more can you wish for? I believe this may in fact be the correct answer here.* 



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gplon13/blog_qq_paulovitordamodarosa.jpg)***Paulo Vitor Damo da Rosa**: We actually discussed that question yesterday! It's a tough one. We couldn't come to an agreement, but I think I'd pick [Grisly Spectacle](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Grisly+Spectacle).* 

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gplon13/blog_qq_raphaellevy.jpg)***Raphaël Lévy**: [Death's Approach](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Death%27s+Approach). People hate it, but come on, it's a one mana removal spell!* 




---



Round 9 Feature Match – Thomas Enevoldsen vs. Martin Jůza
---------------------------------------------------------


*by David Sutcliffe*

 

"My deck's really not very good", Martin Jůza shared with me, on his first visit to the feature match area here in London, "I went to 5-0 then met a couple of good decks and dropped to 5-2. I'm just happy to be here!"


That at least explained why we had seen little of Jůza so far in this Grand Prix but his opponent, Thomas Enevoldsen, was also an unknown quantity. Always one to fish for information before a match, Jůza asked his opponent if he liked his deck.


"I don't think it's very good," Enevoldsen confided, after a pause to consider his words "unless I draw from the good half!"


"So that's something, at least"


The two players were 'on the bubble' with 6-2 records. A win would keep them alive for the last round, while a defeat would send them crashing out of the Grand Prix.


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gplon13/Round-9-Juza.jpg)*Martin Jůza*
 

Jůza won the dice roll but agonised over his mulligan option, before sending his original seven cards away, banking on having six that were better. The Czech star seemed to get his wish, with a Simic draw that rolled out with [Zameck Guildmage](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zameck+Guildmage) and an [Elusive Krasis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elusive+Krasis), although Jůza was reluctant to send his Guildmage into the red zone to trade with Enevoldsen's [Daring Skyjek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daring+Skyjek). A [Truefire Paladin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Truefire+Paladin) joined the Skyjek and Jůza was forced onto the defense – a [Slaughterhorn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Slaughterhorn) added a +1/+1 counter to Jůza's [Elusive Krasis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elusive+Krasis), but all of his creatures remained home on defense.


Enevoldsen played an Ordrunn Veteran, threatening to build a fearsome Battalion of flyers and First and Double strikers, while Jůza missed his fourth land drop for a second turn and passed his turn.


The Dane wasted little time in sending his Battalion into the red zone – this would now be a test of the two player's combat tricks. Jůza's [Elusive Krasis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elusive+Krasis) blocked the Ordrunn Veteran, trading the two creatures away, before Enevoldsen replaced his minotaur with a [Warmind Infantry](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Warmind+Infantry). Jůza summoned a [Disciple of the Old Ways](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Disciple+of+the+Old+Ways) to his defense, but Enevoldsen simply attacked again with his three creatures. This time the [Disciple of the Old Ways](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Disciple+of+the+Old+Ways) offered to trade First Strike damage with the [Truefire Paladin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Truefire+Paladin), and the [Slaughterhorn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Slaughterhorn) to trade with the [Warmind Infantry](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Warmind+Infantry). Revealing [Martial Glory](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Martial+Glory), Enevoldsen ensured that his [Truefire Paladin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Truefire+Paladin) would survive with +0/+3, and that his [Daring Skyjek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daring+Skyjek) would push through six damage with +3/+0.


The Czech star as battered down to 6 life, and while Enevoldsen had a steady supply of creatures to rebuild his Battalion and attack again, Jůza simply couldn't find a fourth land to fight back, and the Dane took to the first game with his next large assault.


Thomas Enevoldsen 1 – 0 Martin Jůza


Was that the good half of Enevoldsen's deck, or had Jůza simply been dreadfully unlucky with his land draws? At the start of the second game the Czech pro's body language suggested he was much happier with his hand, and this time it was the Dane's turn to think long and hard before mulliganing down to six.


[Forest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Forest) from Jůza's Gruul deck.


[Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island) from Enevoldsen's... Boros deck? Wait, what?



![Crocanura](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Crocanura)

[Forest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Forest) again, then [Forest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Forest) and [Verdant Haven](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Verdant+Haven) from Jůza, while Enevoldsen played a second [Island](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Island), a [Forest](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Forest) and a [Crocanura](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crocanura)!


"How did I not notice that you changed decks?!?" Jůza asked, grinning at Enevoldsen's trick "this deck is better?"


"I've spent all day switching between the two", the Dane explained


Jůza found a fourth turn [Zhur-Taa Swine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zhur-Taa+Swine) to begin the offense, while across the table Enevoldsen added a [Crowned Ceratok](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crowned+Ceratok) to his surprise green team. [Agoraphobia](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Agoraphobia) kept the Ceratok at home when the [Zhur-Taa Swine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zhur-Taa+Swine) came calling, and Jůza followed up with an [Elusive Krasis](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Elusive+Krasis), although the Krasis found itself Mugged after blocked Enevoldsen's 2/4 [Crocanura](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crocanura).


The Ceratok blocked the [Zhur-Taa Swine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zhur-Taa+Swine) on the next pass, and now it was the Swine vs [Crocanura](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crocanura), before Enevoldsen dropped a hefty 6/6 [Rubblehulk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rubblehulk)! That gave Jůza a long pause before he said 'ok' to allow the [Rubblehulk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rubblehulk) to resolve, then immediately sent the 'hulk to the top of Enevoldsen's library with [Totally Lost](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Totally+Lost). The Swine attacked again and Enevoldsen took it on the chin, dropping to 10 life, then Jůza added a [Slaughterhorn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Slaughterhorn) to his army.


Enevoldsen replayed his [Rubblehulk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rubblehulk), then followed it up a turn later with an even bigger bomb – Prime-Speaker Zagana arrived in play with six +1/+1 counters, and Enevoldsen sucked up a whole new hand! If a 6/6 [Rubblehulk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rubblehulk) and 7/7 Prime-Speaker weren't enough of a problem, their arrival had also swelled the [Crocanura](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crocanura) to an incredible 6/8!


The game had become incredibly one-sided, with the once-mighty [Zhur-Taa Swine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zhur-Taa+Swine) now completely outgunned. Jůza pondered briefly before sending the Swine into the attack – it was a suicide mission for the poor [Zhur-Taa Swine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zhur-Taa+Swine), but the sheer audacity of the play made Enevoldsen think twice: what tricks did Jůza have up his sleeve – was it safe it block, or was it suicide to let the Swine through?


In the end, Enevoldsen decided to leave nothing to chance and both the [Rubblehulk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rubblehulk) and Prime-Speaker Zegana blocked the [Zhur-Taa Swine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zhur-Taa+Swine). The Swine exploded into fragments, but Jůza then played his own rare – a [Diluvian Primordial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Diluvian+Primordial) that cast the [Mugging](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mugging) from Enevoldsen's graveyard to finish [Rubblehulk](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Rubblehulk) off. Jůza's Swine hadn't died in vain, but the fight was still heading against the Czech star, and Enevoldsen swelled his ranks with a Nightveil Spectre and [Disciple of the Old Ways](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Disciple+of+the+Old+Ways).



![Slaughterhorn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Handlers/Image.ashx?type=card&name=Slaughterhorn)

Attack was Jůza's only form of defence, and this time he sent both the [Slaughterhorn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Slaughterhorn) and [Diluvian Primordial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Diluvian+Primordial) into the fray. Enevoldsen sent his [Crocanura](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crocanura) to swat down the Primordial, and his [Disciple of the Old Ways](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Disciple+of+the+Old+Ways) to slay [Slaughterhorn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Slaughterhorn). Jůza threw a Bloodrush [Skarrg Goliath](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Skarrg+Goliath) onto his [Diluvian Primordial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Diluvian+Primordial), dealing 7 Trample damage over the [Crocanura](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Crocanura) – that put Enevoldsen down to the 3 life, but when the Dane played a 6/6 [Nimbus Swimmer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Nimbus+Swimmer) as a flying blocker, it seemed like the game was up.


Jůza played a [Deathcult Rogue](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathcult+Rogue) that would prove little help against Enevoldsen's creatures then sat back, head in his hands in a picture of defeat as Enevoldsen swung in for the kill, with the Dane playing a Bloodrush [Scab-Clan Charger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scab-Clan+Charger) to ensure his victo... Ætherise! Ætherise! Ætherise!


Jůza's slumped body language had been a trick to convince Enevoldsen to come in with everything, and the Dane had taken the bait! Enevoldsen pulled his creatures back to hand, and now that three mana spent on [Scab-Clan Charger](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Scab-Clan+Charger) seemed particularly painful as it meant he didn't have mana to replay his creatures!


A [Duskmantle Seer](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Duskmantle+Seer) chump-blocked Jůza's Primordial Seer to buy a turn, but despite replaying his Prime-Speaker Zegana to draw even more cards Enevoldsen couldn't find anything to stop Jůza's [Deathcult Rogue](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Deathcult+Rogue) from finishing the job.


Thomas Enevoldsen 1 – 1 Martin Jůza


What a game! Enevoldsen had suckered Jůza with his switch into Simic, only to be suckered himself by the hail mary Ætherise! To be fair, the Dane had hinted that his deck came in two halves... that early piece of mind games now seemed surprisingly honest.


The question now: would Enevoldsen go back to Boros or remain with his bomb-heavy Simic deck in the third game?


![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gplon13/Round-9-Enevoldsen.jpg)*Thomas Enevoldsen*
 

The answer was immediately obvious as the Dane flew out of the blocks with a [Daring Skyjek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Daring+Skyjek), aiming a [Mugging](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Mugging) at Jůza's [Slaughterhorn](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Slaughterhorn) then despatching a [Zhur-Taa Swine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zhur-Taa+Swine) with [Aerial Maneuver](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Aerial+Maneuver) to make his Daring Skyjeck a 4/2 First Striker. Missing plays for a couple of turns put Jůza onto the ropes against the lone Skyjek and all the Czech star could do was throw down a second [Zhur-Taa Swine](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Zhur-Taa+Swine) as it appeared on top of his library.


That was a blocker, but Enevoldsen had the answer already in hand – he enchanted a land with [Debtor's Pulpit](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Debtor%27s+Pulpit), and ensured that the penniless Swine was tapped down while his Skyjek finished the job. After an epic back-and-forth second game, the match was decided in a blowout third game, as the Dane returned to his Boros roots.


**Thomas Enevoldsen 2 – 1 Martin Jůza**




---



Saturday, 11:35 p.m. – Quick Question: Pick Your Rare
-----------------------------------------------------


*by Tobi Henke*

 

Which rare or mythic from Gatecrash would you most want to have in your next sealed pool?



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gplon13/blog_qq_eliaswatsfeldt.jpg)***Elias Watsfeldt**: Mythics, too? Well, in that case ... I'm still going to go with [Clan Defiance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Clan+Defiance).* 

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gplon13/blog_qq_dennizrachid.jpg)***Denniz Rachid**: [Molten Primordial](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Molten+Primordial), also known as "the bus." It's big, it picks people up, and then ... you just win, generally on the same turn when you cast it.* 



![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gplon13/blog_qq_paulovitordamodarosa.jpg)***Paulo Vitor Damo da Rosa**: The most amazing cards are all gold, so there's a good chance they end up in your sideboard. But assuming you can play it, it's [Clan Defiance](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Clan+Defiance). Though not by much. A lot of the rares are very close in their powerlevel, which is nice.* 

![](https://media.magic.wizards.com/image_legacy_migration/mtg/images/daily/events/gplon13/blog_qq_raphaellevy.jpg)***Raphaël Lévy**: [Consuming Aberration](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Card/Details.aspx?name=Consuming+Aberration). I like that guy, he's really, really strong.* 




---



Saturday, 11:44 p.m. – Undefeated Decks
---------------------------------------


*by Event Coverage Staff*

 

Here we got all the decks that made it through the first nine rounds without a single loss. At the very top, the format appeared to be split between rather streamlined Boros decks and more multicolor-oriented green decks, with Gruul somewhere inbetween. The best example of an extremely aggressive Boros deck was piloted by Pierre Pigeon, while on the other end of the spectrum Fabrizio Anteri ran the tables with an honest-to-goodness Golgari deck. No kidding.







#### Pierre Pigeon, 9-0


##### 






![](https://web.archive.org/web/20160726232508im_/http://magic.wizards.com/sites/all/modules/features/wiz_bean_content_deck_list/icons/decklist_download.png)

##### 2 (11)



2
[Wojek Halberdiers](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BWojek%5D+%5BHalberdiers%5D)


1
[Daring Skyjek](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BDaring%5D+%5BSkyjek%5D)


1
[Syndic of Tithes](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BSyndic%5D+%5Bof%5D+%5BTithes%5D)


2
[Skinbrand Goblin](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BSkinbrand%5D+%5BGoblin%5D)


1
[Boros Charm](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BBoros%5D+%5BCharm%5D)


1
[Martial Glory](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BMartial%5D+%5BGlory%5D)


1
[Aerial Maneuver](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BAerial%5D+%5BManeuver%5D)


1
[Blind Obedience](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BBlind%5D+%5BObedience%5D)


1
[Madcap Skills](http://gatherer.wizards.com/Pages/Search/Default.aspx?name=+%5BMadcap%5D+%5BSkills%5D)
